## Section 001: Plugin Settings Configuration Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Settings Configuration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names the theme without its governing artifact, a gitignored .claude/plugin-name.local.md file whose YAML frontmatter carries structured configuration and whose markdown body carries prompts or task context
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Settings Configuration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the plugin-settings skill defines the file location, the frontmatter-plus-body structure, the user-managed lifecycle, and the reading surfaces, hooks, commands, and agents
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Settings Configuration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: without the pattern a plugin scatters state across ad hoc JSON files or hardcodes behavior, losing per-project configurability and the enabled-flag kill switch
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Settings Configuration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference operationalizes per-project plugin settings files, not user-level settings.json or plugin manifest configuration
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Settings Configuration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open with the file location contract, the two-part structure, and the three reading surfaces so every later section hangs off one artifact
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Settings Configuration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the pattern deliberately splits machine and human halves, frontmatter is for bash parsers while the body is for Claude itself, ralph-loop literally feeds the body back as the next prompt

## Section 003: Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed scoreboard scores corpus hygiene while the corpus's load-bearing settings rules go unranked, quick-exit when the file is absent, honor the enabled flag, default every missing field, and update atomically via temp file plus move
- **supporting_reason:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because real-world-examples extracts exactly those four as best practices from both production plugins, and the skill's own sections prescribe each

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed registry lists generic synthesis failures while the corpus names five concrete settings anti-patterns, hardcoded absolute paths, unquoted variables, non-atomic sed -i updates, missing defaults, and ignoring the --- in-body edge case
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because real-world-examples closes with exactly that anti-patterns section, each with a BAD and GOOD pair drawn from the production hooks
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an agent screening against only the seed's three generic rows would pass a hook that corrupts its state file when interrupted mid-sed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the registry catalogs settings-specific failure shapes and their replacements, not general prose defects
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to append the five corpus anti-patterns with their replacements, project-relative paths, quoted expansions, temp-file-plus-move, ${VAR:-default} fallbacks, and the awk body parser that counts markers
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that four of the five are one-line diffs visible in review, only the missing-default failure hides until a field goes empty at runtime, which is why the corpus pairs it with validation
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed gate lists one repository verifier while the corpus supplies concrete settings gates, count the --- markers, regex-validate numeric fields, whitelist enum values, and echo parsed values to stderr under set -x
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because parsing-techniques' validation and debugging sections prescribe marker counting, ^[0-9]+$ checks, case-statement whitelists, and stderr echo of every parsed field
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a settings file passing only visual inspection can still carry a malformed frontmatter block that silently parses to empty strings
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the gates prove settings files and their parsers are checkable, they do not validate the plugin's business logic
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the corpus gates, structural marker count of at least two, per-field type validation with defaults on failure, enum whitelisting via case, and a debug mode printing parsed values
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the corpus's gates run inside the consuming script rather than as a separate linter, validation is a runtime posture because users hand-edit these files between restarts

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide says when to open this reference but not the corpus's surface rule, hooks parse settings with bash, commands read them with the Read tool and can create them, and agents adapt behavior by checking the file in their instructions
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill's reading-settings section gives each surface its own recipe, bash sed pipelines for hooks, Read-tool steps for commands, and instruction-level checks for agents
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an author porting the bash recipe into an agent prompt wastes the agent's native file reading, and one expecting a hook to use the Read tool misunderstands hook execution
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide routes usage of this reference and the surface decision for settings consumers, not agent architecture at large
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the surface fork, deterministic event-time checks parse in hook bash, interactive workflows read and create settings via commands, and adaptive agents check the file as part of their instructions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that creation flows one way, the corpus only ever creates settings from commands and setup scripts, never from hooks, hooks are readers and updaters of fields but the schema is born interactively
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to let commands own creation and templates, hooks own high-frequency reads with quick-exit, and agents own adaptive interpretation of the same file
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the skill's reading-settings section gives each surface its own recipe, bash sed pipelines for hooks, Read-tool steps for commands, and instruction-level checks for agents
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; an author porting the bash recipe into an agent prompt wastes the agent's native file reading, and one expecting a hook to use the Read tool misunderstands hook execution
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the guide routes usage of this reference and the surface decision for settings consumers, not agent architecture at large
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add the surface fork, deterministic event-time checks parse in hook bash, interactive workflows read and create settings via commands, and adaptive agents check the file as part of their instructions

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a journey starting at parsing code produces a schema shaped by sed convenience instead of user needs
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the scenario frames who opens this reference and where in the pipeline they stand, not the full plugin-development journey

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide weighs adopt, adapt, avoid without the corpus's two named tradeoffs, sed/grep versus yq for parsing, and settings-file toggles versus hooks.json edits for activation control
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because parsing-techniques closes its yq section with a pros, cons, and recommendation block, and the skill's temporarily-active-hooks pattern exists precisely to avoid restart-requiring hooks.json edits
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: defaulting to yq adds an install dependency that may be absent, while defaulting to hooks.json edits forces a restart for every toggle
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide covers parsing tooling and activation control for this theme, not plugin architecture at large
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add both forks, sed/grep for simple flat fields with yq reserved for lists and nesting, and settings-file enabled flags for anything users toggle more than rarely
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that both forks trade the same currency, dependency weight against expressiveness, the corpus consistently picks the zero-dependency side and documents the escape hatch
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to parse flat fields with sed and grep, reach for yq only when lists or nested structures appear, and gate hook activity on the settings file rather than hooks.json presence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because parsing-techniques closes its yq section with a pros, cons, and recommendation block, and the skill's temporarily-active-hooks pattern exists precisely to avoid restart-requiring hooks.json edits
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; defaulting to yq adds an install dependency that may be absent, while defaulting to hooks.json edits forces a restart for every toggle
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the guide covers parsing tooling and activation control for this theme, not plugin architecture at large
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add both forks, sed/grep for simple flat fields with yq reserved for lists and nesting, and settings-file enabled flags for anything users toggle more than rarely
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies both forks trade the same currency, dependency weight against expressiveness, the corpus consistently picks the zero-dependency side and documents the escape hatch
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model bounds source counts without the corpus's operational load shape, settings files are read on every hook fire, so parsing sits on the hot path and the corpus optimizes for it explicitly
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because parsing-techniques' performance section prescribes caching the frontmatter in one variable and lazy-loading, cheap jq checks before any file I/O
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a hook that re-parses the file per field or parses before cheap tool-name filters pays file I/O on every tool call in the session
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the model sizes settings-layer work per hook fire, not plugin workload at large
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to model workload as fires times fields, with the two corpus valves, parse-once caching of the frontmatter block and lazy-exit ordering that checks tool relevance before touching the file
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the quick-exit pattern is a workload statement, the common case is designed to be a stat call and exit 0, which is why both production hooks put it in their first lines

## Section 019: Reliability Target

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a settings layer without the atomic guarantee corrupts state exactly when sessions are interrupted, the moment state matters most
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: targets cover the settings file layer, plugin business-logic reliability is out of scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to set targets as zero crashes from missing or malformed files, zero partial writes, and every degradation visible as a stderr warning
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the posture is defaults-as-contract, the parser's fallback values are promises the README template must match, so reliability review is a diff between template values and parser defaults

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guidance classifies verification failures without the corpus's loop-control policy, ralph-loop bounds retries with max_iterations, detects completion via an exact promise string, and deletes its state file to terminate
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the stop hook checks iteration against max_iterations before continuing, compares the extracted promise text exactly, and removes the file on both termination paths
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a loop without the iteration bound retries forever when the completion promise never appears, the exact runaway the max_iterations field exists to stop
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guidance governs settings-driven retry loops, external service retries belong to other references
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to adopt the ralph triad, a counter field incremented atomically per attempt, a bounded maximum with a documented unlimited sentinel, and an explicit completion detector that tears down state
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the state file is the backpressure mechanism itself, deleting it is both stop signal and cleanup, which makes the loop's off switch crash-safe, a dead loop leaves no armed state behind
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to bound every settings-driven loop with a max field, increment before re-arming, and delete state on every exit path
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the stop hook checks iteration against max_iterations before continuing, compares the extracted promise text exactly, and removes the file on both termination paths

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a hook re-running sed on the file for each of five fields multiplies I/O five-fold on every fire in the session
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the method verifies settings-layer efficiency, plugin logic performance is out of scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to verify by inspecting parsers for the three levers, single FRONTMATTER capture, jq-based input filters ahead of file access, and the two-line existence exit

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed statement bounds reference usage without the corpus's scale edges, flat key-value frontmatter parsed by sed, single-writer mutation, per-project scope, and yq as the escape hatch when structure outgrows grep
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because parsing-techniques recommends sed for simple fields and yq for complex structures, and every corpus mutation is a single hook rewriting its own file
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: pushing nested YAML through the grep pipelines silently extracts wrong values, and adding a second writer invites the corruption the atomic rule cannot prevent across processes
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the statement bounds the settings-file pattern, larger state needs different machinery
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the edges, flat fields only for sed parsing, one writer per field, one file per plugin per project, and structure beyond lists moves to yq or another store
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the pattern's ceiling is social as much as technical, these files are meant to be hand-editable by users, a schema too complex to hand-edit has left the pattern's design space regardless of parser power
